	<entry>
		<id>https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Knute_Rockne&amp;diff=687424967&amp;oldid=687424819</id>
		<title>Knute Rockne</title>
		<link rel="alternate" type="text/html" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Knute_Rockne&amp;diff=687424967&amp;oldid=687424819"/>
				<updated>2015-10-25T14:29:20Z</updated>
		
		<summary type="html">&lt;p&gt;‎&lt;span dir=&quot;auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;autocomment&quot;&gt;Notre Dame coach&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;table class='diff diff-contentalign-left'&gt;
				&lt;col class='diff-marker' /&gt;
				&lt;col class='diff-content' /&gt;
				&lt;col class='diff-marker' /&gt;
				&lt;col class='diff-content' /&gt;

				&lt;td colspan='2' style=&quot;background-color: white; color:black; text-align: center;&quot;&gt;← Previous revision&lt;/td&gt;

				&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; class=&quot;diff-lineno&quot;&gt;Line 50:&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; class=&quot;diff-lineno&quot;&gt;Line 50:&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f9f9f9; color: #333333; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #e6e6e6; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f9f9f9; color: #333333; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #e6e6e6; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f9f9f9; color: #333333; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #e6e6e6; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;[[File:Notre Dame Box.svg|thumb|left|220px|The Notre Dame Box]]&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f9f9f9; color: #333333; font-size: 88%; border-
1000
style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #e6e6e6; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;[[File:Notre Dame Box.svg|thumb|left|220px|The Notre Dame Box]]&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;−&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color:black; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;Rockne took over from his predecessor [[Jesse Harper]] in the war-torn season of [[1918 Notre Dame Fighting Irish football team|1918]], posting a 3&amp;amp;ndash;1&amp;amp;ndash;2 record, losing only to the [[1918 Michigan Agricultural Aggies football team|Michigan Aggies]]. In the backfield was [[Leonard Bahan]], [[George Gipp]], and [[Curly Lambeau]]. With Gipp, Rockne had an ideal handler of the [[forward pass]].&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://books.google.com/books?id=_RqQQHqQdAAC&amp;amp;pg=PA98&amp;amp;lpg=PA98#v=onepage&amp;amp;q&amp;amp;f=false&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://books.google.com/books?id=-W1JAQAAMAAJ&amp;amp;pg=PA662#v=onepage&amp;amp;q&amp;amp;f=false&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; The [[1919 Notre Dame Fighting Irish football team|1919 team]] went undefeated and were a national champion. Gipp died December 14, 1920, just two weeks after being elected Notre Dame's first All-American by Walter Camp. Gipp likely contracted [[Streptococcal pharyngitis|strep throat]] and pneumonia while giving [[Punt (gridiron football)|punting]] lessons after his final game, November 20 against Northwestern University. Since [[antibiotics]] were not available in the 1920s, treatment options for such infections were limited and they could be fatal even to young, healthy individuals. It was while on his hospital bed and speaking to Rockne &lt;del class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;hat&lt;/del&gt; &lt;del class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;He&lt;/del&gt; is purported to have delivered the famous,&quot;win just one for the Gipper&quot; line.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;Keyes 2006&quot;&amp;gt;{{Cite book&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;+&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color:black; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;Rockne took over from his predecessor [[Jesse Harper]] in the war-torn season of [[1918 Notre Dame Fighting Irish football team|1918]], posting a 3&amp;amp;ndash;1&amp;amp;ndash;2 record, losing only to the [[1918 Michigan Agricultural Aggies football team|Michigan Aggies]]. In the backfield was [[Leonard Bahan]], [[George Gipp]], and [[Curly Lambeau]]. With Gipp, Rockne had an ideal handler of the [[forward pass]].&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://books.google.com/books?id=_RqQQHqQdAAC&amp;amp;pg=PA98&amp;amp;lpg=PA98#v=onepage&amp;amp;q&amp;amp;f=false&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://books.google.com/books?id=-W1JAQAAMAAJ&amp;amp;pg=PA662#v=onepage&amp;amp;q&amp;amp;f=false&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; The [[1919 Notre Dame Fighting Irish football team|1919 team]] went undefeated and were a national champion. Gipp died December 14, 1920, just two weeks after being elected Notre Dame's first All-American by Walter Camp. Gipp likely contracted [[Streptococcal pharyngitis|strep throat]] and pneumonia while giving [[Punt (gridiron football)|punting]] lessons after his final game, November 20 against Northwestern University. Since [[antibiotics]] were not available in the 1920s, treatment options for such infections were limited and they could be fatal even to young, healthy individuals. It was while on his hospital bed and speaking to Rockne &lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;that&lt;/ins&gt; &lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;he&lt;/ins&gt; is purported to have delivered the famous,&quot;win just one for the Gipper&quot; line.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;K
1000
eyes 2006&quot;&amp;gt;{{Cite book&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;

1000
ys a [[contemporary Christian music|Christian pop]] style of [[Christian hip hop]] and [[Christian electronic dance music]] with some [[Christian rock]]. Hollyn was a contestant on [[American Idol (season 12)|season 12 of ''American Idol'']], where she made it to the Hollywood rounds. She has released one [[extended play]], ''Hollyn'' in 2015, with [[Gotee Records]]. &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

		<summary type="html">&lt;p&gt;‎&lt;span dir=&quot;auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;autocomment&quot;&gt;Daylight saving time: &lt;/span&gt;Cleanup&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f9f9f9; color: #333333; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #e6e6e6; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;First observation of DST was in 1931, but only for the state of [[Baja California]]. It used the &quot;Hora del Centro&quot; from April 1st to September 30th, and the &quot;Hora del Oeste&quot; the rest of the year.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;conuee&quot; /&amp;gt; Until 1996, Baja California was the only Mexican state to observe DST, coinciding with the observance of DST across the border in [[San Diego, California]].&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f9f9f9; color: #333333; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #e6e6e6; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;First observation of DST was in 1931, but only for the state of [[Baja California]]. It used the &quot;Hora del Centro&quot; from April 1st to September 30th, and the &quot;Hora del Oeste&quot; the rest of the year.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;conuee&quot; /&amp;gt; Until 1996, Baja California was the only Mexican state to observe DST, coinciding with the observance of DST across the border in [[San Diego, California]].&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f9f9f9; color: #333333; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #e6e6e6; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;−&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color:black; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;[[Daylight saving time]] has been observed in Mexico beginning in 1996.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;[http://www.timeanddate.com/worldclock/timezone.html?n=155&amp;amp;syear=1990 Mexico City time changes in 1996]&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; &lt;del class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;Except for the&lt;/del&gt; municipalities located less than 20 km from the US border,&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;border&quot;&amp;gt;[http://www.timeanddate.com/news/time/north-mexico-dst-change.html Northern Mexican Border's New Daylight Saving Plan]&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; it &lt;del class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;does not coincide&lt;/del&gt; with the [[Energy Policy Act of 2005#Change to daylight saving time|longer extended daylight saving period adopted for 2007 in the United States]].  &lt;del class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;Rather,&lt;/del&gt; the &lt;del class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;federal&lt;/del&gt; &lt;del class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;law&lt;/del&gt; &lt;del class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;dictates&lt;/del&gt; &lt;del class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;that&lt;/del&gt; daylight saving time &lt;del class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;be&lt;/del&gt; observed between 2 a.m. on the first Sunday in April through 2 a.m. on the last Sunday in October.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;[http://www.conae.gob.mx/wb/CONAE/CONA_924_periodo_de_aplicacio National Commission for the Conservation of Energy]&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;+&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color:black; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;[[Daylight saving time]] has been observed in Mexico beginning in 1996.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;[http://www.timeanddate.com/worldclock/timezone.html?n=155&amp;amp;syear=1990 Mexico City time changes in 1996]&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; &lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;For&lt;/ins&gt; municipalities located less than 20 km from the US border&lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;, such as [[Ciudad Juarez]], and the entire state of Baja California (Norte)&lt;/ins&gt;,&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;border&quot;&amp;gt;[http://www.timeanddate.com/news/time/north-mexico-dst-change.html Northern Mexican Border's New Daylight Saving Plan]&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; it &lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;coincides&lt;/ins&gt; with the [[Energy Policy Act of 2005#Change to daylight saving time|longer extended daylight saving period adopted for 2007 in the United States]].  &lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;But in&lt;/ins&gt; the &lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;rest&lt;/ins&gt; &lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;of&lt;/ins&gt; &lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;the&lt;/ins&gt; &lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt;country,&lt;/ins&gt; daylight saving time &lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffcha
1000
nge-inline&quot;&gt;is&lt;/ins&gt; observed between 2 a.m. on the first Sunday in April through 2 a.m. on the last Sunday in October.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;[http://www.conae.gob.mx/wb/CONAE/CONA_924_periodo_de_aplicacio National Commission for the Conservation of Energy]&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;ins class=&quot;diffchange diffchange-inline&quot;&gt; Quintana Roo and Sonora states do not observe DST.&lt;/ins&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f9f9f9; color: #333333; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #e6e6e6; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f9f9f9; color: #333333; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #e6e6e6; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f9f9f9; color: #333333; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #e6e6e6; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;As the United States now starts DST on the second Sunday in March and ends it on the first Sunday in November, Mexico's time zones are out of synchronization with American and Canadian time zones for two periods each year. The first is the three or four &amp;lt;!-- See talk for explanation --&amp;gt; weeks between the second Sunday in March and the first Sunday in April. The second is the single week between the last Sunday in October and the first Sunday in November.  During these periods, clocks in Mexico City match those in [[Denver]] rather than those in [[Chicago]].  The [[Mexican Stock Exchange]] changes its hours during these periods in order to maintain synchronization with the U.S. markets. Conversely, television schedules are not changed for these situations, meaning Mexican television networks which are carried directly by American cable and satellite services have their programming aired an hour ahead or behind in the United States during these interregnums.&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f9f9f9; color: #333333; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #e6e6e6; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;As the United States now starts DST on the second Sunday in March and ends it on the first Sunday in November, Mexico's time zones are out of synchronization with American and Canadian time zones for two periods each year. The first is the three or four &amp;lt;!-- See talk for explanation --&amp;gt; weeks between the second Sunday in March and the first Sunday in April. The second is the single week between the last Sunday in October and the first Sunday in November.  During these periods, clocks in Mexico City match those in [[Denver]] rather than those in [[Chicago]].  The [[Mexican Stock Exchange]] changes its hours during these periods in order to maintain synchronization with the U.S. markets. Conversely, television schedules are not changed for these situations, meaning Mexican television networks which are carried directly by American cable and satellite services have their programming aired an hour ahead or behind in the United States during these interregnums.&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
